transliteration">Kam-siok</span></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #b0c4de;">Tibetan name</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Tibetan_alphabet" title="Tibetan alphabet">Tibetan</a></th><td><span class="uchen" lang="bo" style="font-size:1.25em; vertical-align:top; word-wrap: break-word;">&#3904;&#3923;&#3851;&#3942;&#3956;&#3936;&#3956;&#3851;</span></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><table class="collapsible collapsed" style="padding:0;border:none;margin:-3px;width:auto;min-width:100%;font-size:100%;clear:none;float:none;background-color:transparent"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;font-size: 100%; text-align: left; background-color: #f9ffbc;">Transcriptions</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Wylie_transliteration" title="Wylie transliteration">Wylie</a></th><td><span lang="bo-Latn" style="font-style:normal" title="Standard Tibetan-language transliteration">kan su\'u<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></span></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Gansu</b> (<span lang="zh-Hans"><span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gansu.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ee/Gansu.ogg" title="Gansu.ogg">&#29976;&#32899;</a></span></span></span>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Postal_romanization" title="Postal romanization">formerly romanised</a> as <b>Kansu</b>) is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Provinces_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Provinces of the People\'s Republic of China">province of the People\'s Republic of China</a>, located in the <a href="/wiki/Northwest_China" title="Northwest China">northwest</a> of the country.\n</p><p>It lies between the <a href="/wiki/Tibetan_Plateau" title="Tibetan Plateau">Tibetan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Loess_Plateau" title="Loess Plateau">Loess</a> plateaus, and borders <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Govi-Altai_Province" title="Govi-Altai Province">Govi-Altai Province</a>), <a href="/wiki/Inner_Mongolia" title="Inner Mongolia">Inner Mongolia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ningxia" title="Ningxia">Ningxia</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qinghai" title="Qinghai">Qinghai</a> to the west, <a href="/wiki/Sichuan" title="Sichuan">Sichuan</a> to the south, and <a href="/wiki/Shaanxi" title="Shaanxi">Shaanxi</a> to the east. The <a href="/wiki/Yellow_River" title="Yellow River">Yellow River</a> passes through the southern part of the province.\n</p><p>Gansu has a population of 26 million (as of 2009) and covers an area of 453,700 square kilometres (175,200&#160;sq&#160;mi).  The capital is <a href="/wiki/Lanzhou" title="Lanzhou">Lanzhou</a>, located in the southeast part of the province.\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_Qin" title="State of Qin">State of Qin</a> originated in what is now southeastern Gansu, and went on to form the first dynasty of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imperial_China" title="Imperial China">Imperial China</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Northern_Silk_Road" title="Northern Silk Road">Northern Silk Road</a> ran through the <a href="/wiki/Hexi_Corridor" title="Hexi Corridor">Hexi Corridor</a>, which passes through Gansu.\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" <span class="toctext">Anti-desertification project</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#Space_launch_center"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">Space launch center</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">17</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Gansu is a compound of the names of <a href="/wiki/Ganzhou_District" title="Ganzhou District">Ganzhou</a> (now a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/District_(PRC)" title="District (PRC)">district</a> of <a href="/wiki/Zhangye" title="Zhangye">Zhangye</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Suzhou_District" title="Suzhou District">Suzhou</a>, the seat of <a href="/wiki/Jiuquan" title="Jiuquan">Jiuquan</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prefecture_(PRC)" title="Prefecture (PRC)">Prefecture</a>, formerly the two most important Chinese settlements in the area.\n</p><p>Gansu is abbreviated as "<span lang="zh"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E7%94%98" title="wikt:&#29976;">&#29976;</a></span>" (<i lang="zh-Latn" title="Chinese-language transliteration">G&#257;n</i>) or "<span lang="zh-hans"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E9%99%87" title="wikt:&#38471;">&#38471;</a></span>" (<i lang="zh-Latn" title="Chinese-language transliteration">L&#466;ng</i>), and is also known as Longxi (<span lang="zh-Hans">&#38471;&#35199;</span>; ""[land] west of Long"") or Longyou (<span lang="zh-Hans">&#38471;&#21491;</span>; ""[land] right of Long""), in reference to the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Long_Mountain_(China)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Long Mountain (China) (page does not exist)">Long Mountain</a> east of Gansu.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Summer_Vacation_2007,_263,_Watchtower_In_The_Morning_Light,_Dunhuang,_Gansu_Province.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2561" decoding="async" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Summer_Vacation_2007%2C_263%2C_Watchtower_In_The_Morning_Light%2C_Dunhuang%2C_Gansu_Province.jpg/250px-Summer_Vacation_2007%2C_263%2C_Watchtower_In_The_Morning_Light%2C_Dunhuang%2C_Gansu_Province.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Summer_Vacation_2007%2C_263%2C_Watchtower_In_The_Morning_Light%2C_Dunhuang%2C_Gansu_Province.jpg/375px-Summer_Vacation_2007%2C_263%2C_Watchtower_In_The_Morning_Light%2C_Dunhuang%2C_Gansu_Province.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Summer_Vacation_2007%2C_263%2C_Watchtower_In_The_Morning_Light%2C_Dunhuang%2C_Gansu_Province.jpg/500px-Summer_Vacation_2007%2C_263%2C_Watchtower_In_The_Morning_Light%2C_Dunhuang%2C_Gansu_Province.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Summer_Vacation_2007,_263,_Watchtower_In_The_Morning_Light,_Dunhuang,_Gansu_Province.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The ruins of a <a href="/wiki/Han_dynasty" title="Han dynasty">Han dynasty</a> (202 BC&#8211;220 AD) Chinese <a href="/wiki/Watchtower" title="Watchtower">watchtower</a> made of <a href="/wiki/Rammed_earth" title="Rammed earth">rammed earth</a> at <a href="/wiki/Dunhuang" title="Dunhuang">Dunhuang</a>, Gansu province, the eastern edge of the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Gansu&#8217;s name is a <a href="/wiki/Compound_(linguistics)" title="Compound (linguistics)">compound name</a> first used during the <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">Song dynasty</a> of two <a href="/wiki/Sui_dynasty" title="Sui dynasty">Sui</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty" title="Tang dynasty">Tang dynasty</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2014)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_administrative_divisions_of_China" title="History of the administrative divisions of China">prefectures</a> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#24030;</span>): Gan (around <a href="/wiki/Zhangye" title="Zhangye">Zhangye</a>) and Su (around <a href="/wiki/Jiuquan" title="Jiuquan">Jiuquan</a>). Its eastern part forms part of one of the cradles of ancient Chinese civilisation.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_Gansu">Ancient Gansu</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Ancient Gansu">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chinese_jar,_Neolithic_period,_painted_earthenware,_HAA.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1290" data-file-width="1239" decoding="async" height="229" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Chinese_jar%2C_Neolithic_period%2C_painted_earthenware%2C_HAA.JPG/220px-Chinese_jar%2C_Neolithic_period%2C_painted_earthenware%2C_HAA.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Chinese_jar%2C_Neolithic_period%2C_painted_earthenware%2C_HAA.JPG/330px-Chinese_jar%2C_Neolithic_period%2C_painted_earthenware%2C_HAA.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Chinese_jar%2C_Neolithic_period%2C_painted_earthenware%2C_HAA.JPG/440px-Chinese_jar%2C_Neolithic_period%2C_painted_earthenware%2C_HAA.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chinese_jar,_Neolithic_period,_painted_earthenware,_HAA.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Xindian_culture" title="Xindian culture">Xindian culture</a> era jar with two lug handles uncovered in Gansu, dating to around 1,000 BC</div></div></div>\n<p>In prehistoric times, Gansu was host to <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> cultures. The <a href="/wiki/Dadiwan_culture" title="Dadiwan culture">Dadiwan culture</a>, from where archaeologically significant <a href="/wiki/Artifact_(archaeology)" title="Artifact (archaeology)">artifacts</a> have been excavated, flourished in the eastern end of Gansu from about 6000<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>BC to about 3000<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Majiayao_culture" title="Majiayao culture">Majiayao culture</a> and part of the <a href="/wiki/Qijia_culture" title="Qijia culture">Qijia culture</a> took root in Gansu from 3100 BC to 2700 BC and 2400 BC to 1900 BC respectively.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Yuezhi" title="Yuezhi">Yuezhi</a> originally lived in the very western part of Gansu until they were forced to emigrate by the <a href="/wiki/Xiongnu" title="Xiongnu">Xiongnu</a> around 177 BCE.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Qin_(state)" title="Qin (state)">State of Qin</a>, later to become the <a href="/wiki/Qin_dynasty" title="Qin dynasty">founding state</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Early_Imperial_China" title="Early Imperial China">Chinese empire</a>, grew out from the southeastern part of Gansu, specifically the <a href="/wiki/Tianshui" title="Tianshui">Tianshui</a> area. The Qin name is believed to have originated, in part, from the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Qin tombs and artifacts have been excavated from <a href="/wiki/Fangmatan" title="Fangmatan">Fangmatan</a> near Tianshui, including one 2200-year-old map of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guixian_County" title="Guixian County">Guixian County</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Imperial_era">Imperial era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Imperial era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yumenguan.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1007" data-file-width="1519" decoding="async" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Yumenguan.jpg/250px-Yumenguan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Yumenguan.jpg/375px-Yumenguan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Yumenguan.jpg/500px-Yumenguan.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Yumenguan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The ruins of a gate at <a href="/wiki/Yumen_Pass" title="Yumen Pass">Yumen Pass</a>, built during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jin_Dynasty_(265-420)" title="Jin Dynasty (265-420)">Jin Dynasty (265-420)</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In imperial times, Gansu was an important strategic outpost and communications link for the Chinese empire, as the <a href="/wiki/Hexi_Corridor" title="Hexi Corridor">Hexi Corridor</a> runs along the "neck" of the province. The <a href="/wiki/Han_dynasty" title="Han dynasty">Han dynasty</a> extended the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Great_Wall_of_China" title="History of the Great Wall of China">Great Wall</a> across this corridor, building the strategic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yumenguan" title="Yumenguan">Yumenguan</a> (Jade Gate Pass, near <a href="/wiki/Dunhuang" title="Dunhuang">Dunhuang</a>) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangguan" title="Yangguan">Yangguan</a> fort towns along it. Remains of the wall and the towns can be found there. The <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a> built the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jiayuguan_(pass)" title="Jiayuguan (pass)">Jiayuguan</a> outpost in Gansu. To the west of Yumenguan and the <a href="/wiki/Qilian_Mountains" title="Qilian Mountains">Qilian Mountains</a>, at the northwestern end of the province, the <a href="/wiki/Yuezhi" title="Yuezhi">Yuezhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wusun" title="Wusun">Wusun</a>, and other <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomadic</a> tribes dwelt (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shiji" title="Shiji">Shiji</a> 123), occasionally figuring in regional imperial Chinese <a href="/wiki/Geopolitics" title="Geopolitics">geopolitics</a>.\n</p><p>By the Qingshui treaty, concluded in 823 between the <a href="/wiki/Tibetan_Empire" title="Tibetan Empire">Tibetan Empire</a> and the Tang dynasty, China lost much of western Gansu province for a significant period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Uyghur_Khaganate" title="Uyghur Khaganate">Uyghur Khaganate</a>, a Buddhist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yugur_people" title="Yugur people">Yugur</a> (Uyghur) state called the <a href="/wiki/Ganzhou_Uyghur_Kingdom" title="Ganzhou Uyghur Kingdom">Ganzhou Uyghur Kingdom</a> was established by migrating Uyghurs from the Khaganate in part of Gansu that lasted from 848 to 1036<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>AD.\n</p><p>Along the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a>, Gansu was an economically important province, as well as a cultural transmission path. Temples and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> <a href="/wiki/Grotto" title="Grotto">grottoes</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> such as those at <a href="/wiki/Mogao_Caves" title="Mogao Caves">Mogao Caves</a> (\'Caves of the Thousand Buddhas\') and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maijishan_Caves" title="Maijishan Caves">Maijishan Caves</a> contain artistically and historically revealing <a href="/wiki/Mural" title="Mural">murals</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> An early form of paper inscribed with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_writing" title="Chinese writing">Chinese characters</a> and dating to about 8<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>BC was discovered at the site of a Western Han <a href="/wiki/Garrison" title="Garrison">garrison</a> near the Yumen pass in August 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The province was also the origin of the <a href="/wiki/Dungan_Revolt_(1862%E2%80%9377)" title="Dungan Revolt (1862&#8211;77)">Dungan Revolt</a> of 1862-77. Among the <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing</a> forces were Muslim generals, including <a href="/wiki/Ma_Zhan%27ao" title="Ma Zhan\'ao">Ma Zhan\'ao</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ma_Anliang" title="Ma Anliang">Ma Anliang</a>, who helped the Qing crush the rebel Muslims. The revolt had spread into Gansu from neighbouring Qinghai.\n</p><p>There was another <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dungan_revolt_(1895%E2%80%931896)" title="Dungan revolt (1895&#8211;1896)">Dungan revolt from 1895 to 1896</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JiayuguanFort.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1095" data-file-width="1762" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/JiayuguanFort.jpg/250px-JiayuguanFort.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/JiayuguanFort.jpg/375px-JiayuguanFort.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/JiayuguanFort.jpg/500px-JiayuguanFort.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:JiayuguanFort.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jiayuguan_Pass" title="Jiayuguan Pass">Jiayuguan</a> Fort</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Republican_China">Republican China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Republican China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>As a result of frequent earthquakes, droughts and famines, the economic progress of Gansu was significantly slower than that of other provinces of China until recently. Based on the area\'s abundant mineral resources it has begun developing into a vital industrial center. An <a href="/wiki/1920_Haiyuan_earthquake" title="1920 Haiyuan earthquake">earthquake in Gansu</a> at 8.6 on the <a href="/wiki/Richter_magnitude_scale" title="Richter magnitude scale">Richter scale</a> killed around 180,000 people mostly in the present-day area of <a href="/wiki/Ningxia" title="Ningxia">Ningxia</a> in 1920, and <a href="/wiki/1932_Changma_earthquake" title="1932 Changma earthquake">another with a magnitude of 7.6</a> killed 275 in 1932.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NGDC_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-NGDC-13">[13]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim_Conflict_in_Gansu_(1927%E2%80%931930)" title="Muslim Conflict in Gansu (1927&#8211;1930)">Muslim Conflict in Gansu (1927&#8211;1930)</a> was a conflict against the <a href="/wiki/Guominjun" title="Guominjun">Guominjun</a>.\n</p><p>While the Muslim General <a href="/wiki/Ma_Hongbin" title="Ma Hongbin">Ma Hongbin</a> was acting chairman of the province, Muslim General <a href="/wiki/Ma_Buqing" title="Ma Buqing">Ma Buqing</a> was in virtual control of Gansu in 1940. Liangzhou District in <a href="/wiki/Wuwei,_Gansu" title="Wuwei, Gansu">Wuwei</a> was previously his headquarters in Gansu, where he controlled 15 million Muslims.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a> came under <a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">Kuomintang</a> (Nationalist) control after their soldiers entered via Gansu.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lin2010_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lin2010-15">[15]</a></sup> Gansu\'s Tienshui was the site of a Japanese-Chinese warplane fight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Armstrong2006_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Armstrong2006-16">[16]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Gansu was vulnerable to Soviet penetration via Xinjiang.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fleming2014_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fleming2014-17">[17]</a></sup> Gansu was a passageway for Soviet supplies during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Second Sino-Japanese War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forbes1986_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes1986-18">[18]</a></sup> Lanzhou was a destination point via a road coming from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dihua" title="Dihua">Dihua</a> (&#220;r&#252;mqi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kataoka1974_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kataoka1974-19">[19]</a></sup> Lanzhou and <a href="/wiki/Lhasa" title="Lhasa">Lhasa</a> were designated to be recipients of a new railway.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (July 2017)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ginsburgs2013_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ginsburgs2013-20">[20]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kuomintang_Islamic_insurgency_in_China_(1950%E2%80%931958)" title="Kuomintang Islamic insurgency in China (1950&#8211;1958)">Kuomintang Islamic insurgency in China (1950&#8211;1958)</a> was a prolongation of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a> in several provinces including Gansu.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gansu_Donkeys.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2164" data-file-width="2492" decoding="async" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cc/Gansu_Donkeys.jpg/220px-Gansu_Donkeys.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cc/Gansu_Donkeys.jpg/330px-Gansu_Donkeys.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cc/Gansu_Donkeys.jpg/440px-Gansu_Donkeys.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gansu_Donkeys.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Semi-arid land, suitable for light grazing</div></div></div>\n<p>Gansu has an area of 454,000 square kilometres (175,000&#160;sq&#160;mi), and the vast majority of its land is more than 1,000 metres (3,300&#160;ft) above <a href="/wiki/Sea_level" title="Sea level">sea level</a>. It lies between the <a href="/wiki/Tibetan_Plateau" title="Tibetan Plateau">Tibetan Plateau</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Loess_Plateau" title="Loess Plateau">Loess Plateau</a>, bordering <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Govi-Altai_Province" title="Govi-Altai Province">Govi-Altai Province</a>) to the northwest, <a href="/wiki/Inner_Mongolia" title="Inner Mongolia">Inner Mongolia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ningxia" title="Ningxia">Ningxia</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Shaanxi" title="Shaanxi">Shaanxi</a> to the east, <a href="/wiki/Sichuan" title="Sichuan">Sichuan</a> to the south, and <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a> to the west. The <a href="/wiki/Yellow_River" title="Yellow River">Yellow River</a> passes through the southern part of the province. The province contains the <a href="/wiki/Geographical_centre" title="Geographical centre">geographical centre</a> of China, marked by the Center of the Country Monument at <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Gansu&amp;params=35_50_40.9_N_103_27_7.5_E_region:CN-62_type:landmark&amp;title=Geographical+centre+of+China"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">35&#176;50&#8242;40.9&#8243;N</span> <span class="longitude">103&#176;27&#8242;7.5&#8243;E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#65279; / &#65279;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="vcard"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">35.844694&#176;N 103.452083&#176;E</span><span style="display:none">&#65279; / <span class="geo">35.844694; 103.452083</span></span><span style="display:none">&#65279; (<span class="fn org">Geographical centre of China</span>)</span></span></span></a></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Part of the <a href="/wiki/Gobi_Desert" title="Gobi Desert">Gobi Desert</a> is located in Gansu, as well as small parts of the <a href="/wiki/Badain_Jaran_Desert" title="Badain Jaran Desert">Badain Jaran Desert</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Tengger_Desert" title="Tengger Desert">Tengger Desert</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Yellow_River" title="Yellow River">Yellow River</a> gets most of its water from Gansu, flowing straight through Lanzhou. The area around Wuwei is part of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Shiyang_River_Basin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Shiyang River Basin (page does not exist)">Shiyang River Basin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The landscape in Gansu is very mountainous in the south and flat in the north. The mountains in the south are part of the <a href="/wiki/Qilian_Mountains" title="Qilian Mountains">Qilian Mountains</a>, while the far western <a href="/wiki/Altyn-Tagh" title="Altyn-Tagh">Altyn-Tagh</a> contains the province&#8217;s highest point, at 5,830 metres (19,130&#160;ft).\n</p><p>A natural land passage known as <a href="/wiki/Hexi_Corridor" title="Hexi Corridor">Hexi Corridor</a>, stretching some 1,000 kilometres (620&#160;mi) from Lanzhou to the <a href="/wiki/Yumen_Pass" title="Yumen Pass">Jade Gate</a>, is situated within the province. It is bound from north by the Gobi Desert and Qilian Mountains from the south.\n</p><p>Gansu generally has a semi-arid to arid continental climate (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K&#246;ppen climate classification">K&#246;ppen</a> <i>BSk</i> or <i>BWk</i>) with warm to hot summers and cold to very cold winters, although <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diurnal_temperature_range" title="Diurnal temperature range">diurnal temperature ranges</a> are often so large that maxima remain above 0&#160;&#176;C (32&#160;&#176;F) even in winter.  However, due to extreme altitude, some areas of Gansu exhibit a <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">subarctic climate</a> (<i>Dwc</i>) &#8211; with winter temperatures sometimes dropping to &#8722;40&#160;&#176;C (&#8722;40&#160;&#176;F). Most of the limited precipitation is delivered in the summer months: winters are so dry that snow cover is confined to very high altitudes and the <a href="/wiki/Snow_line" title="Snow line">snow line</a> can be as high as 5,500 metres (18,040&#160;ft) in the southwest.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="width:; max-width:908px;">\n<div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Daxia-River-Valley-panorama-5902%2B5903%2B5904%2B5905%2B5906.jpg" title="Panorama of the lower Daxia River valley in the northeast of the Linxia County, and the loess plateau flanking in, cut by a canyon"><img alt="" data-file-height="1483" data-file-width="6737" decoding="async" height="198" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Daxia-River-Valley-panorama-5902%2B5903%2B5904%2B5905%2B5906.jpg/900px-Daxia-River-Valley-panorama-5902%2B5903%2B5904%2B5905%2B5906.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Daxia-River-Valley-panorama-5902%2B5903%2B5904%2B5905%2B5906.jpg/1350px-Daxia-River-Valley-panorama-5902%2B5903%2B5904%2B5905%2B5906.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Daxia-River-Valley-panorama-5902%2B5903%2B5904%2B5905%2B5906.jpg/1800px-Daxia-River-Valley-panorama-5902%2B5903%2B5904%2B5905%2B5906.jpg 2x" width="900"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Daxia-River-Valley-panorama-5902%2B5903%2B5904%2B5905%2B5906.jpg" title="File:Daxia-River-Valley-panorama-5902+5903+5904+5905+5906.jpg"> </a></div>Panorama of the lower <a href="/wiki/Daxia_River" title="Daxia River">Daxia River</a> valley in the northeast of the <a href="/wiki/Linxia_County" title="Linxia County">Linxia County</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loess_plateau" title="Loess plateau">loess plateau</a> flanking in, cut by a <a href="/wiki/Canyon" title="Canyon">canyon</a></div>\n</div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_administrative_divisions_of_Gansu" title="List of administrative divisions of Gansu">List of administrative divisions of Gansu</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_township-level_divisions_of_Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="List of township-level divisions of Gansu (page does not exist)">List of township-level divisions of Gansu</a></div>\n<p>Gansu is divided into fourteen <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_China#Prefectural_level" title="Administrative divisions of China">prefecture-level divisions</a>: twelve <a href="/wiki/Prefecture-level_city" title="Prefecture-level city">prefecture-level cities</a> and two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autonomous_prefectures_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Autonomous prefectures of the People\'s Republic of China">autonomous prefectures</a>:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="margin:1em auto 1em auto; width:90%; font-size:smaller; text-align:center">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="12"><b>Administrative divisions of Gansu</b>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="12" style="font-size:larger"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gansu_prfc_map.png"><img alt="Gansu prfc map.png" data-file-height="545" data-file-width="612" decoding="async" height="401" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Gansu_prfc_map.png/450px-Gansu_prfc_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/59/Gansu_prfc_map.png 1.5x" width="450"/></a>\n<p><span style="background-color:#7C9973; color:black; border:1px solid darkgray; href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China" title="Communist Party of China">CPC</a> Gansu Committee</b>: The Secretary of the CPC Gansu Committee is the highest-ranking office within Gansu Province.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-xinhua_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-xinhua-29">[28]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Zhang_Desheng" title="Zhang Desheng">Zhang Desheng</a> (<span lang="zh-Hans" text">&#32993;&#32487;&#23447;</span>): 1966&#8722;1967</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Xian_Henghan" title="Xian Henghan">Xian Henghan</a> (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language 1977&#8722;1981</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Feng_Jixin" title="Feng Jixin">Feng Jixin</a> (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#20911;&#32426;&#26032;</span>): 1981&#8722;1983</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Li_Ziqi" title="Li Ziqi">Li Ziqi</a> (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#26446;&#23376;&#22855;</span>): 1983&#8722;1990</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gu_Jinchi" title="Gu Jinchi">Gu Jinchi</a> (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#39038;&#37329;&#27744;</span>): 1990&#8722;1993</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Yan_Haiwang" Ying</a> (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#23385;&#33521;</span>): 1998&#8722;2001</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Song_Zhaosu" title="Song Zhaosu">Song Zhaosu</a> (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#23435;&#29031;&#32899;</span>): 2001&#8722;2003</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Su_Rong" title="Su Rong">Su Rong</a> (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#29579;&#19977;&#36816;</span>): December 2011 &#8722; March 2017</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lin_Duo" title="Lin Duo">Lin Duo</a> (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#26519;&#38094;</span>): March 2017 &#8722; incumbent</li></ol>\n<p><b>Governors of Gansu</b>: The Governorship of Gansu is the second highest-ranking official within Gansu, behind the Secretary of the CPC Gansu Committee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-xinhua_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-xinhua-29">[28]</a></sup> The governor is responsible for all issues related to <a href="/wiki/Economics" title="Economics">economics</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Personnel" title="Personnel">personnel</a>, political initiatives, the <a href="/wiki/Environmental_policy" title="Environmental policy">environment</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_policy" title="Foreign policy">foreign affairs</a> of the province.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-xinhua_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-xinhua-29">[28]</a></sup> The Governor is appointed by the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu_Provincial_People%27s_Congress&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gansu Provincial People\'s Congress (page does not exist)">Gansu Provincial People\'s Congress</a>, which is the province\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative" title="Legislative">legislative</a> body.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-xinhua_29-3"><a href="#cite_note-xinhua-29">[28]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Wang_Shitai" title="Wang Shitai">Wang Shitai</a> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#29579;&#19990;&#27888;</span>): 1949&#8722;1950</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Deng_Baoshan" title="Deng Baoshan">Deng Baoshan</a> (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#37011;&#23453;&#22999;</span>): 1950&#8722;1967</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Xian_Henghan" title="Xian Henghan">Xian Henghan</a> (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#20924;&#24658;&#27721;</span>): 1967&#8722;1977</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Song_Ping" title="Song Ping">Song Ping</a> (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#36158;&#24535;&#26480;</span>): 1986&#8722;1993</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Yan_Haiwang" title="Yan Haiwang">Yan Haiwang</a> (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#38414;&#28023;&#26106;</span>): 1993</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Zhang_Wule" title="Zhang Wule">Zhang Wule</a> (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#24352;&#21566;&#20048;</span>): 1993&#8722;1996</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sun_Ying" title="Sun Ying">Sun Ying</a> (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#23385;&#33521;</span>): 1996&#8722;1998</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Song_Zhaosu" title="Song Zhaosu">Song Zhaosu</a> (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#23435;&#29031;&#32899;</span>): 1998&#8722;2001</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lu_Hao_(born_1947)" title="Lu Hao (born 1947)">Lu Hao</a> (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#38470;&#28009;</span>): 2001&#8722;2006</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Xu_Shousheng" title="Xu Shousheng">Xu Shousheng</a> (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#24464;&#23432;&#30427;</span>): January 2007&#8722;July 2010<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-xinhua_29-4"><a href="#cite_note-xinhua-29">[28]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Liu_Weiping" title="Liu Weiping">Liu Weiping</a> (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#21016;&#20255;&#24179;</span>): July 2010&#8722;April 2016</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lin_Duo" title="Lin Duo">Lin Duo</a> (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#26519;&#38094;</span>): April 2016&#8722;April 2017</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tang_Renjian" title="Tang Renjian">Tang Renjian</a> (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#21776;&#20161;&#20581;</span>): April 2017&#8722;incumbent</li></ol>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lanzhou-rio-amarillo-baita-shan-d03.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Lanzhou-rio-amarillo-baita-shan-d03.jpg/220px-Lanzhou-rio-amarillo-baita-shan-d03.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Lanzhou-rio-amarillo-baita-shan-d03.jpg/330px-Lanzhou-rio-amarillo-baita-shan-d03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Lanzhou-rio-amarillo-baita-shan-d03.jpg/440px-Lanzhou-rio-amarillo-baita-shan-d03.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lanzhou-rio-amarillo-baita-shan-d03.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Yellow River in Lanzhou seen from the park of the White Pagoda.</div></div></div>\n<p>Agricultural production includes <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Linseed_oil" title="Linseed oil">linseed oil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Melons" title="Melons">melons</a> (such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Honeydew_melon" title="Honeydew melon">honeydew melon</a>, known locally as the <a href="/wiki/Bailan_melon" title="Bailan melon">Bailan melon</a> or "Wallace" due to its introduction by US <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vice_president_of_the_United_States" title="Vice president of the United States">vice president</a> <a href="/wiki/Henry_A._Wallace" title="Henry A. Wallace">Henry A. Wallace</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a>.  Gansu is known as a source for wild medicinal herbs which are used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_medicine" title="Chinese medicine">Chinese medicine</a>. However, pollution by heavy metals, such as <a href="/wiki/Cadmium_poisoning" title="Cadmium poisoning">cadmium</a> in irrigation water, has resulted in the poisoning of many acres of agricultural land. The extent and nature of the heavy metal pollution is considered a state secret.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caixin030113_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Caixin030113-31">[30]</a></sup>\n</p><p>However, most of Gansu\'s economy is based on <a href="/wiki/Mining" title="Mining">mining</a> and the extraction of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minerals" title="Minerals">minerals</a>, especially <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rare_earth_elements" title="Rare earth elements">rare earth elements</a>.  The province has significant deposits of <a href="/wiki/Antimony" title="Antimony">antimony</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chromium" title="Chromium">chromium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cobalt" title="Cobalt">cobalt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fluorite" title="Fluorite">fluorite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gypsum" title="Gypsum">gypsum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iridium" title="Iridium">iridium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iron" title="Iron">iron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lead" title="Lead">lead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(element)" title="Mercury (element)">mercury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mirabilite" title="Mirabilite">mirabilite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nickel" title="Nickel">nickel</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crude_oil" title="Crude oil">crude oil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Platinum" title="Platinum">platinum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Troilite" title="Troilite">troilite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tungsten" title="Tungsten">tungsten</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a> among others.  The oil fields at Yumen and Changqing are considered significant.\n</p><p>Gansu has China\'s largest nickel deposits accounting for over 90% of China\'s total nickel reserves.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>Industries other than mining include <a href="/wiki/Electricity_generation" title="Electricity generation">electricity generation</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petrochemicals" title="Petrochemicals">petrochemicals</a>, oil exploration machinery, and building materials.\n</p><p>According to some sources, the province is also a center of China\'s nuclear industry.\n</p><p>Despite recent growth in Gansu and the booming economy in the rest of China, Gansu is still considered to be one of the poorest provinces in China. Its nominal GDP for 2011 was about 502.0 billion yuan (79.69 billion USD) and per capita of 12,836&#160;RMB (1,879&#160;USD). Tourism has been a bright spot in contributing to Gansu\'s overall economy. As mentioned below, Gansu offers a wide variety of choices for national and international tourists.\n</p><p>As stipulated in the country\'s 12th Five Year Plan, the local government of Gansu hopes to grow the provinces GDP by 10% annually by focusing investments on five pillar industries: renewable energy, coal, chemicals, nonferrous metals, pharmaceuticals and services.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_and_technological_development_zones">Economic and technological development zones</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Economic and technological development zones">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The following economic and technological zones are situated in Gansu:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Lanzhou National Economic and Technological Development Zone was established in 1993, located in the center of Lanzhou Anning District. The zone has a planned area of 9.53&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (3.68&#160;sq&#160;mi). 17 colleges, 11 scientific research institutions, 21 large and medium-size companies and other 1735 enterprises have been set up in the zone. Main industries include textile mills, rubber, fertilizer plants, oil refinery, petrochemical, machinery, and metallurgical industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Lanzhou New &amp; Hi-Tech Industrial Development Zone, Lanzhou Hi-Tech Industrial Development Zone, one of the first 27 national hi-tech industrial development zones, was established in 1998 covering more than 10&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (3.9&#160;sq&#160;mi). It is expected to expand another 19&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (7.3&#160;sq&#160;mi). The zone mainly focuses on Biotechnology, chemical industry, building decoration materials and information technology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:5674-Linxia-City-Xin-Xi-Lu.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/5674-Linxia-City-Xin-Xi-Lu.jpg/220px-5674-Linxia-City-Xin-Xi-Lu.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/5674-Linxia-City-Xin-Xi-Lu.jpg/330px-5674-Linxia-City-Xin-Xi-Lu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/5674-Linxia-City-Xin-Xi-Lu.jpg/440px-5674-Linxia-City-Xin-Xi-Lu.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:5674-Linxia-City-Xin-Xi-Lu.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>On the streets of <a href="/wiki/Linxia_City" title="Linxia City">Linxia</a></div></div></div>\n<table style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+14.3%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census2000_42-0"><a style="text-align:right;padding:1px">25,575,254</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+1.8%</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left">Ningxia Province/AR was part of Gansu Province until 1929 and 1954-1958.</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Gansu province is home to 30,711,287 people. Most of the population, 73%, is rural. Gansu is 92% <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Han</a> and also has <a href="/wiki/Hui_people" title="Hui people">Hui</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tibetan_people" title="Tibetan people">Tibetan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dongxiang_people" title="Dongxiang people">Dongxiang</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tu_(ethnic_group)" title="Tu (ethnic group)">Tu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yugur" title="Yugur">Yugur</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bonans" title="Bonans">Bonan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongols" title="Mongols">Mongolian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salar_people" title="Salar people">Salar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kazakhs" title="Kazakhs">Kazakh</a> minorities. Gansu province\'s community of Chinese <a href="/wiki/Hui_people" title="Hui people">Hui</a> Muslims was bolstered by Hui Muslims resettled from <a href="/wiki/Shaanxi" title="Shaanxi">Shaanxi</a> province during the <a href="/wiki/Dungan_Revolt_(1862%E2%80%9377)" title="Dungan Revolt (1862&#8211;77)">Dungan Revolt</a>.  Gansu is also a historical home, along with <a href="/wiki/Shaanxi" title="Shaanxi">Shaanxi</a>, of the <a href="/wiki/Dungan_language" title="Dungan language">dialect</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Dungan_people" title="Dungan people">Dungans</a>, who migrated to <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>. The southwestern corner of Gansu is home to a large <a href="/wiki/Tibetan_people" title="Tibetan people">ethnic Tibetan</a> population.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Most of the inhabitants of Gansu speak dialects of Northern <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese" title="Mandarin Chinese">Mandarin Chinese</a>. On the border areas of Gansu one might encounter <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tu_language" title="Tu language">Tu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amdo" title="Amdo">Amdo Tibetan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_language" title="Mongolian language">Mongolian</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_language" title="Kazakh language">Kazakh language</a>. Most of the minorities also speak Chinese.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Gansu" title="Music of Gansu">Music of Gansu</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gansu_Sheep.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2109" data-file-width="3048" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Gansu_Sheep.jpg/220px-Gansu_Sheep.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Gansu_Sheep.jpg/330px-Gansu_Sheep.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Gansu_Sheep.jpg/440px-Gansu_Sheep.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gansu_Sheep.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sheep grazing beside a main road near <a href="/wiki/Jiuquan" title="Jiuquan">Jiuquan</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The cuisine of Gansu is based on the staple crops grown there: <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barley" title="Barley">barley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beans" title="Beans">beans</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sweet_potatoes" title="Sweet potatoes">sweet potatoes</a>.  Within China, Gansu is known for its <a href="/wiki/Lamian" title="Lamian">lamian</a> (pulled noodles), and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Islamic_cuisine" title="Chinese Islamic cuisine">Muslim restaurants</a> which feature authentic Gansu cuisine.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright" style=""><div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px">\n<div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black">\n<div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:DarkOrchid"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:DodgerBlue"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 3978.0357839777px; border-left-color:Green"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Green"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Green"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 410.83968437179px; border-left-color:Yellow"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Yellow"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Yellow"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 106.48918403248px; border-left-color:Honeydew"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Honeydew"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Honeydew"></div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<p>Religion in Gansu (2012)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CFPS2012_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-CFPS2012-44">[43]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Honeydew; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Non religious and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_folk_religion" title="Chinese folk religion">traditional faiths</a> (88%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Yellow; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_China" title="Buddhism in China">Buddhism</a> (8.2%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Green; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Islam_in_China" title="Islam in China">Islam</a> (3.4%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_China" title="Protestantism in China">Protestantism</a> (0.4%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DarkOrchid; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">Catholicism</a> (0.1%)</div>\n</div>\n</div></div>\n<p>According to a 2012 survey<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CFPS2012_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-CFPS2012-44">[43]</a></sup> only around 12% of the population of Gansu belongs to organised religions, the largest groups being <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_China" title="Buddhism in China">Buddhists</a> with 8.2%, followed by <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_China" title="Islam in China">Muslims</a> with 3.4%, <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_China" title="Protestantism in China">Protestants</a> with 0.4% and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholicism_in_China" title="Catholicism in China">Catholic</a> with 0.1% (in total, as of 2012 Christians comprise 0.5% of the population, decreasing from 1.02% in 2004<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup>) Around 88% of the population may be either irreligious or involved in <a href="/wiki/Chinese_folk_religion" title="Chinese folk religion">worship of nature deities</a>, Buddhism, <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a>, Taoism, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_salvationist_religions" title="Chinese salvationist religions">folk religious sects</a>.\n</p><p>Muslim restaurants are known as "qingzhen restaurants" ("pure truth restaurants"), and feature typical Chinese dishes, but without any pork products, and instead an emphasis on <a href="/wiki/Lamb_and_mutton" title="Lamb and mutton">lamb and mutton</a>. Gansu has many works of <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhist</a> art, including the <a href="/wiki/Maijishan_Grottoes" title="Maijishan Grottoes">Maijishan Grottoes</a>. Dunhuang was a major centre of Buddhism in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>.\n</p>\n<table>\n<tbody><tr>\n<td><ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed" class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yulin_Cave_3_w_wall_Manjusri_(Western_Xia).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2185" data-file-width="1461" decoding="async" height="329" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Yulin_Cave_3_w_wall_Manjusri_%28Western_Xia%29.jpg/440px-Yulin_Cave_3_w_wall_Manjusri_%28Western_Xia%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Yulin_Cave_3_w_wall_Manjusri_(Western_Xia).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A painting of the Buddhist <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manjusri" title="Manjusri">manjusri</a></i>, from the <a href="/wiki/Yulin_Caves" title="Yulin Caves">Yulin Caves</a> of Gansu, <a href="/wiki/Tangut_people" title="Tangut people">Tangut</a>-led <a href="/wiki/Western_Xia" title="Western Xia">Western Xia</a> dynasty (1038-1227 AD)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Han_Dynasty_Granary_west_of_Dunhuang.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1717" data-file-width="4519" decoding="async" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Han_Dynasty_Granary_west_of_Dunhuang.jpg/440px-Han_Dynasty_Granary_west_of_Dunhuang.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Han_Dynasty_Granary_west_of_Dunhuang.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>These <a href="/wiki/Rammed_earth" title="Rammed earth">rammed earth</a> ruins of a <a href="/wiki/Granary" title="Granary">granary</a> in Hecang Fortress (<a href="/wiki/Simplified_Chinese_characters" title="Simplified Chinese characters">Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh-Hans">&#27827;&#20179;&#22478;&#65307;</span>; <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">H&#233;c&#257;ngch&#233;ng</span></i>), located ~11 km (7 miles) northeast of the Western-Han-era <a href="/wiki/Yumen_Pass" title="Yumen Pass">Yumen Pass</a>, were built during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_Han" title="Western Han">Western Han</a> (202 BC - 9 AD) and significantly rebuilt during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_Jin" title="Western Jin">Western Jin</a> (280-316 AD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jiayuguan_Pass_of_the_Great_Wall">Jiayuguan Pass of the Great Wall</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Jiayuguan Pass of the Great Wall">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jiayuguan_Pass" title="Jiayuguan Pass">Jiayuguan Pass</a></div>\n<p>Jiayuguan Pass, in Jiayuguan city, is the largest and most intact pass, or entrance, of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Wall_of_China" title="Great Wall of China">Great Wall</a>. Jiayuguan Pass was built in the early Ming dynasty, somewhere around the year 1372. It was built near an oasis that was then on the extreme western edge of China. Jiayuguan Pass was the first pass on the west end of the great wall so it earned the name &#8220;The First And Greatest Pass Under Heaven.&#8221;\n</p><p>An extra brick is said to rest on a ledge over one of the gates.  One legend holds that the official in charge asked the designer to calculate how many bricks would be used. The designer gave him the number and when the project was finished, only one brick was left. It was put on the top of the pass as a symbol of commemoration.  Another account holds that the building project was assigned to a military manager and an architect.  The architect presented the manager with a requisition for the total number of bricks that he would need.  When the manager found out that the architect had not asked for any extra bricks, he demanded that the architect make some provision for unforeseen circumstances.  The architect, taking this as an insult to his planning ability, added a single extra brick to the request.  When the gate was finished, the single extra brick was, in fact, extra and was left on the ledge over the gate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNTOLEGEND_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNTOLEGEND-47">[46]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mogao_Grottoes">Mogao Grottoes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Mogao Grottoes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mogao_Caves" title="Mogao Caves">Mogao Caves</a></div>\n<p>The Mogao Grottoes near <a href="/wiki/Dunhuang" title="Dunhuang">Dunhuang</a> have a collection of <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhist</a> art. Originally there were a thousand grottoes, but now only 492 cave temples remain. Each temple has a large statue of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddha_(general)" title="Buddha (general)">buddha</a> or <a href="/wiki/Bodhisattva" title="Bodhisattva">bodhisattva</a> and paintings of religious scenes. In 336&#160;AD, a monk named Le Zun (Lo-tsun) came near Echoing Sand Mountain, when he had a <a href="/wiki/Vision_(spirituality)" title="Vision (spirituality)">vision</a>. He started to carve the first grotto. During the <a href="/wiki/Five_Dynasties_and_Ten_Kingdoms_period" title="Five Dynasties and Ten Kingdoms period">Five Dynasties period</a> they ran out of room on the cliff and could not build any more grottoes.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Silk_Road_and_Dunhuang_City">Silk Road and Dunhuang City</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Silk Road and Dunhuang City">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cernuschi_Museum_20060812_156.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="2304" decoding="async" height="300" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Cernuschi_Museum_20060812_156.jpg/200px-Cernuschi_Museum_20060812_156.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Cernuschi_Museum_20060812_156.jpg/300px-Cernuschi_Museum_20060812_156.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Cernuschi_Museum_20060812_156.jpg/400px-Cernuschi_Museum_20060812_156.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cernuschi_Museum_20060812_156.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A terracotta warrior from Gansu, with traces of polychrome and gold, from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tang_Dynasty" title="Tang Dynasty">Tang Dynasty</a> (618&#8722;907)</div></div></div>\n<p>The historic <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> starts in <a href="/wiki/Chang%27an" title="Chang\'an">Chang\'an</a> and goes to <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a>. On the way merchants would go to Dunhuang in Gansu. In Dunhuang they would get fresh camels, food and guards for the journey around the dangerous <a href="/wiki/Taklamakan_Desert" title="Taklamakan Desert">Taklamakan Desert</a>. Before departing Dunhuang they would pray to the Mogao Grottoes for a safe journey, if they came back alive they would thank the gods at the grottoes. Across the desert they would form a train of camels to protect themselves from thieving bandits. The next stop, <a href="/wiki/Kashgar" title="Kashgar">Kashi (Kashgar)</a>, was a welcome sight to the merchants. At Kashi most would trade and go back and the ones who stayed would eat fruit and trade their <a href="/wiki/Bactrian_camel" title="Bactrian camel">Bactrian camels</a> for <a href="/wiki/Dromedary" title="Dromedary">single humped</a> ones. After Kashi they would keep going until they reached their next destination.\n</p><p>Located about 5&#160;km (3.1&#160;mi) southwest of the city, the <a href="/wiki/Crescent_Lake_(Dunhuang)" title="Crescent Lake (Dunhuang)">Crescent Lake</a> or Yueyaquan is an oasis and popular spot for tourists seeking respite from the heat of the desert. Activities includes camel and 4x4 rides.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Silk_Route_Museum">Silk Route Museum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Silk Route Museum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Silk_Route_Museum" title="Silk Route Museum">Silk Route Museum</a></div>\n<p>The Silk Route Museum is located in <a href="/wiki/Jiuquan" title="Jiuquan">Jiuquan</a> along the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a>, a trading route connecting <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a> to China, used by <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo" title="Marco Polo">Marco Polo</a>. It is also built over the tomb of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Liang_(Sixteen_Kingdoms)" title="Western Liang (Sixteen Kingdoms)">Western Liang</a> King.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-touristlink_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-touristlink-48">[47]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bingling_Temple">Bingling Temple</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Bingling Temple">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bingling_Temple" title="Bingling Temple">Bingling Temple</a></div>\n<p>Bingling Temple, or Bingling Grottoes, is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> cave complex in a canyon along the <a href="/wiki/Yellow_River" title="Yellow River">Yellow River</a>. Begun in 420&#160;AD during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_Jin_Dynasty" title="Western Jin Dynasty">Western Jin Dynasty</a>, the site contains dozens of caves and caverns filled with outstanding examples of carvings, sculpture, and frescoes. The great Maitreya Buddha is more than 27 meters tall and is similar in style to the great Buddhas that once lined the cliffs of <a href="/wiki/Buddhas_of_Bamiyan" title="Buddhas of Bamiyan">Bamiyan</a>, Afghanistan. Access to the site is by boat from <a href="/wiki/Yongjing_County" title="Yongjing County">Yongjing</a> in the summer or fall. There is no other access point.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Labrang_Monastery">Labrang Monastery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Labrang Monastery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Labrang_Monastery" title="Labrang Monastery">Labrang Monastery</a></div>\n<p>Labrang Tashikyil Monastery is located in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xiahe" title="Xiahe">Xiahe County</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gannan_Tibetan_Autonomous_Prefecture" title="Gannan Tibetan Autonomous Prefecture">Gannan Tibetan Autonomous Prefecture</a>, located in the southern part of Gansu, and part of the traditional Tibetan province of <a href="/wiki/Amdo" title="Amdo">Amdo</a>. It is one of the six major monasteries of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gelukpa" title="Gelukpa">Gelukpa</a> tradition of <a href="/wiki/Tibetan_Buddhism" title="Tibetan Buddhism">Tibetan Buddhism</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a>, and the most important one in Amdo. Built in 1710, it is headed by the Jamyang-zhaypa. It has 6 <i>dratsang</i> (colleges), and houses over sixty thousand religious texts and other works of literature as well as other cultural artifacts.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_universities">Colleges and universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Colleges and universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_and_colleges_in_Gansu" title="List of universities and colleges in Gansu">List of universities and colleges in Gansu</a></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Lanzhou_University" title="Lanzhou University">Lanzhou University</a> Lanzhou
