Polytechnic College</a></li>\n<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Northwest_Minority_University&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Northwest Minority University (page does not exist)">Northwest Minority University</a></li>\n<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tianshui_Normal_College&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tianshui Normal College (page does not exist)">Tianshui Normal College</a> (Tianshui)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Longdong_College" title="Longdong College">Longdong College</a> (Qingyang)</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_resources">Natural resources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Natural resources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Land">Land</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Land">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li>166,400 square kilometres (64,200&#160;sq&#160;mi) grassland</li>\n<li>46,700 square kilometres (18,000&#160;sq&#160;mi) mountain slopes suitable for livestock breeding</li>\n<li>46,200 square kilometres (17,800&#160;sq&#160;mi) forests (standing timber reserves of 0.2 cubic kilometres (0.048&#160;cu&#160;mi))</li>\n<li>35,300 square kilometres (13,600&#160;sq&#160;mi) cultivated land (1,400 square metres (15,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) per capita)</li>\n<li>66,600 square kilometres (25,700&#160;sq&#160;mi) wasteland suitable for forestation</li>\n<li>10,000 square kilometres (3,900&#160;sq&#160;mi) wasteland suitable for farming</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Minerals">Minerals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Minerals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Three thousand deposits of 145 different minerals. Ninety-four minerals have been found and ascertained, including nickel, cobalt, platinum, <a href="/wiki/Selenium" title="Selenium">selenium</a>, casting clay, finishing serpentine, and five other minerals whose reserves are the largest in China.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Gansu has advantages in getting nickel, zinc, cobalt, platinum, iridium, copper, barite, and baudisserite.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Among Gansu&#8217;s most important sources of energy are its water resources: the Yellow River and other inland river drainage basins. Gansu is placed ninth among China&#8217;s provinces in annual hydropower potential and water discharge. Gansu produces 17.24 gigawatts of hydropower a year. Twenty-nine hydropower stations have been constructed in Gansu, altogether(?) capable of generating 30 gigawatts. Gansu has an estimated coal reserve of 8.92 billion tons and petroleum reserve of 700 million tons.\n</p><p>There is also good potential for wind and solar power development. The <a href="/wiki/Gansu_Wind_Farm" title="Gansu Wind Farm">Gansu Wind Farm</a> project &#8211; already producing 7.965GW in 2015<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-busitza_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-busitza-49">[48]</a></sup> &#8211; is expected to achieve 20GW by 2020, at which time it will likely become the world\'s biggest collective windfarm.\n</p><p>In November 2017 an agreement between the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Chinese Academy of Sciences">Chinese Academy of Sciences</a> and Gansu government was announced, to site and begin operations of a <a href="/wiki/Molten_salt_reactor" title="Molten salt reactor">molten salt reactor</a> pilot project in the province by 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">Flora and fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Flora and fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Gansu has 659 species of wild animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup> It has twenty-four rare animals which are under a state protection.\n</p><p>Gansu\'s mammals include some of the world\'s most charismatic: the <a href="/wiki/Giant_panda" title="Giant panda">giant panda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden_monkey" title="Golden monkey">golden monkeys</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lynx" title="Lynx">lynx</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snow_leopard" title="Snow leopard">snow leopards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sika_deer" title="Sika deer">sika deer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Musk_deer" title="Musk deer">musk deer</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Bactrian_camel" title="Bactrian camel">Bactrian camel</a>.\n</p><p>Among zoologists who study <a href="/wiki/Mole_(animal)" title="Mole (animal)">moles</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gansu_mole" title="Gansu mole">Gansu mole</a> is of great interest.  For a reason that can only be speculated, it is taxologically a <a href="/wiki/Scalopini" title="Scalopini">New World mole</a> living among <a href="/wiki/Talpinae" title="Talpinae">Old Word moles</a>; that is to say an American mole living in a sea of Euro-Asians.\n</p><p>Gansu is home to 441 <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bird" title="Bird">birds</a>; it is a center of <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemism</a> and home to many species and <a href="/wiki/Subspecies" title="Subspecies">subspecies</a> which occur nowhere else in the world.\n</p><p>Gansu is China\'s second-largest producer of medicinal plants and herbs, including some produced nowhere else, such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hairy_asiabell" title="Hairy asiabell">hairy asiabell</a> root, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fritillary" title="Fritillary">fritillary</a> bulb, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_caterpillar_fungus" title="Chinese caterpillar fungus">Chinese caterpillar fungus</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_disasters">Natural disasters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Natural disasters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/1920_Haiyuan_earthquake" title="1920 Haiyuan earthquake">1920 Haiyuan earthquake</a></div>\n<p>On 16 December 1920, Gansu witnessed the deadliest landslide ever recorded. A series of landslides, triggered by a single earthquake, accounted for most of the 180,000 people killed in the event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anti-desertification_project">Anti-desertification project</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Anti-desertification project">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a> is working with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Forestry_Administration_of_China" title="State Forestry Administration of China">State Forestry Administration of China</a> on the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Silk_Road_Ecosystem_Restoration_project&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Silk Road Ecosystem Restoration project (page does not exist)">Silk Road Ecosystem Restoration project</a>, designed to prevent degradation and desertification in Gansu. It is estimated to cost up to US$150 million.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Space_launch_center">Space launch center</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Space launch center">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Jiuquan_Satellite_Launch_Center" title="Jiuquan Satellite Launch Center">Jiuquan Satellite Launch Center</a>, located in the Gobi desert, is named after the city of <a href="/wiki/Jiuquan" title="Jiuquan">Jiuquan</a>, Gansu, the nearest city, although the center itself is in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inner_Mongolia_Autonomous_Region" title="Inner Mongolia Autonomous Region">Inner Mongolia Autonomous Region</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gansu&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Portal-puzzle.svg"><img alt="Portal-puzzle.svg" class="noviewer" data-file-height="28" transmission of Buddhism">Silk Road transmission of Buddhism</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
